---


**Saturday, 12:07 p.m. - Grand Prix Atlanta Legacy Primer**
-----------------------------------------------------------


*by Steve Sadin and Blake Rasmussen*
There are a TON of good decks to play in Legacy right now. Whether you want to play a fast combo deck, a beatdown deck, or a control deck  there's going to be a good option for you.


So what are we waiting for? Let's take a look at some decklists!


### Reanimator


While Reanimator wasn't a big factor at Grand Prix Indianapolis (the last Legacy Grand Prix), ever since the release of *Avacyn Restored*, [Animate Dead](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Animate+Dead)s and [Entomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Entomb)s have been running rampant at Legacy tournaments across the globe. It's at the point where many pros have confidently stated that "Reanimator is the deck to beat in Legacy".


And there's one big reason for that  [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand).


The premise behind Reanimator is simple. Get a big creature into your graveyard with [Entomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Entomb), or [Careful Study](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Careful+Study)  then bring it back into play with an [Animate Dead](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Animate+Dead), a [Reanimate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reanimate), or an [Exhume](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Exhume).


The deck is blisteringly fast, and thanks to [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze), and [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize), it's far from helpless in the face of your opponent's answers.


Plus, even if your opponent has an answer for your reanimated threat (be it a [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares), a [Terminus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terminus), a [Diabolic Edict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diabolic+Edict), or even a [Pernicious Deed](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pernicious+Deed) with a ton of mana) that won't be good enough... Because you can restock your hand with [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand), you will either draw yourself a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) to counter their answer, or another reanimation spell to bring forth another huge monster a turn later. And once that's happened, it's only a matter of time before you'll fly to victory.







#### Gerry Thompson Reanimator


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Island)


















One last important thing to note about the deck: not even uncounterable graveyard hate like [Faerie Macabre](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Faerie+Macabre) (which, under normal circumstances, would be a great way to stop a Reanimator deck) isn't enough to beat the current iterations of Legacy Reanimator since they can sideboard in [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell)s to bring huge threats into play without them ever touching the graveyard.


### [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets)


Reanimator may be the deck to beat right now, but tempo oriented [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets) decks are more than capable of holding their own in today's metagame. Shuffling up a mixture of cheap, potent, threats backed by mana denial ([Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) and sometimes [Stifle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stifle)), cheap removal ([Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt)s, and [Forked Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forked+Bolt)s), free counterspells ([Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), and [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze)), and [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)s has been a recipe for success for as long as Legacy has been a format. And right now is no exception.


While the deck is capable of executing a lot of quick kills, it also has a lot of staying power. If you have the time to sculpt your hand with [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)s and [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder)s, and protect your threats with [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will)s  then you can beat just about anything with your [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets) deck.







#### Matt Costa RUG Delver


#####

### Stoneblade


Tom Martell won Grand Prix Indianapolis just a few months ago with his take on Stoneblade  a Blue-White-Black (or sometimes just Blue-White) deck full of cheap answers that looks to make exceptionally good use of [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic).


While Stoneblade decks might not be as explosive as Reanimator decks which can put [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand)s into play on turn two  the deck is still capable of some very fast starts (there are a lot of decks that simply can't beat a turn three [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull)), and it's almost impossible to hate out with targeted sideboard cards.


So if you're looking for a resilient control deck that's capable of some quick kills  then Stoneblade may very well be the deck for you.







#### Tom Martell Stoneblade


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

### Other decks with [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will)


While Reanimator, RUG [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets), and Stoneblade are currently the most popular blue decks in Legacy, don't be fooled into thinking that they're your only options. There are tons of other great decks with [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) in them which (while somewhat out of the public eye right now) are still more than capable of dominating a tournament.


### Sneak and Show


So you want to put a [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand), or an [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Emrakul%2C+the+Aeons+Torn) into play on turn two -- but you're worried about [Tormod's Crypt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tormod%27s+Crypt)s and friends ruining your day. Well, fear not, because you can circumvent the graveyard entirely by playing Sneak and Show.


Instead of reanimating threats back from the grave, this deck uses [Sneak Attack](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sneak+Attack), and [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) to put its humongous threats into play. While Sneak and Show decks typically don't have access to black discard spells like [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize), they are still more than capable of pushing their threats through with [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), [Misdirection](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Misdirection), and [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce).







#### Jonathan Hickerson Sneak and Show

### [Hypergenesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hypergenesis)


[Hypergenesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hypergenesis) is another fun, explosive deck that pops up now and then, but has a hard time gaining too much traction in a format full of decks that can [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) it, or easily counter its namesake spell.


The deck is fairly straightforward. Use various methods of acceleration to power out a fast three-mana cascade spell, cascading into [Hypergenesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hypergenesis), the only spell under three mana in the deck. If that resolves, dump all kinds of huge permanents on the board, such as [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Emrakul%2C+the+Aeons+Torn), [Angel of Despair](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Angel+of+Despair), [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) and [Akroma's Memorial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Akroma%27s+Memorial).


The deck is fun and powerful, but suffers from the vulnerability of its key spell to countermagic and the restrictions on casting costs (for Cascade) that keep it from running disruption like [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) or [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek).


But the deck can be a blast to play and is incredibly powerful if [Hypergenesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hypergenesis) resolves. Todd Anderson finished 5th at a SCG Open in Columbus earlier this month with the following list:







#### Todd Anderson Hypergenesis


#####

### Merfolk


Former Legacy standout Merfolk has fallen out of favor recently, but the fact that the deck is full of quick threats (that can grow to huge sizes when surrounded by enough [Lord of Atlantis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lord+of+Atlantis)es, [Merrow Reejerey](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Merrow+Reejerey)s, [Coralhelm Commander](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Coralhelm+Commander)s, and [Phantasmal Image](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantasmal+Image)s)) backed by the free countermagic suite of [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze) and [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), and a great mana base means that Merfolk will always be a viable option.







#### Adam Boyd Merfolk


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

### Blue White Miracles


If you're looking for an already established archetype that can make good use of the recently unbanned [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax)  then look no further than Blue White Miracles. If you want to grind people out with counterspells, clear the board with [Terminus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terminus), and eventually take over the game with a Planeswalker like [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor), or a big [Entreat the Angels](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Entreat+the+Angels)  then you're going to have a tough time finding a more appropriate deck than Blue White Control.


Oh, and don't forget that you can always stash away Miracle cards right at the top of your deck with [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor), and [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top).

### Non [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) decks


But Legacy is not all [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will)s and [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)s. In a format where every non-banned, non-*Unglued* card every printed is legal, one of the most striking features of the format is the variety of viable decks. Each of these decks may not carry the protection that *Alliances* most famous instant packs, but they all have powerful, typically proactive game plans.


### Maverick


First among decks that forgo [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) is Maverick, easily the most successful Legacy archetype to go without blue cards. Maverick is a G/W beatdown and disruption deck centered on [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary) and a host of disruptive beaters like [Qasali Pridemage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Qasali+Pridemage), [Scavenging Ooze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scavenging+Ooze), [Mother of Runes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mother+of+Runes), [Gaddock Teeg](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gaddock+Teeg) and [Thalia, Guardian of Thraben](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thalia%2C+Guardian+of+Thraben). [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch) and [Green Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Green+Sun%27s+Zenith) for [Dryad Arbor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Arbor) gives the deck eight ways to accelerate turn one, but even without those cards the deck operates well at just two mana, which, along with [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary), makes it one of the best [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) decks in the format.


Speaking of which, [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary) gives the deck a surprising amount of play against the field. Searching up [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) is obvious, but the presence of [Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas) makes trying to win with [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Emrakul%2C+the+Aeons+Torn) a losing proposition. [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) adds to the deck's toolbox feel, and access to the format's best removal  [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) and [Path to Exile](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Path+to+Exile)  plus any number of [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte)s gives the deck a leg up in creature matches.


There have been lists that touch on blue mana for [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor) and [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), but by and large Maverick sticks to the G/W formula.

### Dredge


The boogeyman of formats past, Dredge has had some of the bite taken out of its bark by the plethora of graveyard hate played in the format.


For the uninitiated, Dredge is deck that plays almost entirely from its graveyard, milling huge portions of its deck thanks to the Golgari guild's keyword ability that gave the deck its name. Dredge deposits cards like [Golgari Grave-Troll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Grave-Troll) and [Stinkweed Imp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stinkweed+Imp) into the graveyard as a way to mill [Narcomoeba](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Narcomoeba), [Bridge from Below](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bridge+from+Below) and [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy), eventually winning with some number of Bridge-spawned zombie tokens, fatties reanimated with [Dread Return](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dread+Return) and self-returning creatures like [Ichorid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ichorid). It also has access to one of the most powerful cards in the format, [Lion's Eye Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lion%27s+Eye+Diamond).


The success of decks like Reanimator and the incidental damage done to a number of decks by graveyard hate makes cards like [Relic of Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Relic+of+Progenitus), [Tormod's Crypt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tormod%27s+Crypt), [Surgical Extraction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Surgical+Extraction), [Leyline of the Void](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Leyline+of+the+Void) and [Bojuka Bog](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bojuka+Bog) relatively common in Legacy, meaning that one of the best game one decks ever created often has a very difficult time with games two and three.

**Burn**


Mono Red burn decks saw something of a resurgence early this year, outright winning two Star City Games Legacy Opens and placing well after being largely absent from the metagame for a long time.


Burn decks do exactly what their name implies, flinging as much damage at an opponent as fast as possible with a plethora of the best direct damage spells ever printed. [Fireblast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fireblast), [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt), [Goblin Guide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Guide) (one of a very few creatures the deck actually plays), [Price of Progress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Price+of+Progress) and [Chain Lightning](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chain+Lightning) serve as the backbone of a deck that often plays out like something of a combo deck. Find 20 points worth of burn, aim them at your opponent, roast accordingly.


The deck's strengths typically lie in an unprepared metagame, but as a mono colored deck with access to a lot of anti-Blue cards, the deck does have its place in a format defined in large part by [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland), [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) and [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm). Its popularity, which rises and wanes on occasion, can be attributed in part to the Fire and Lightning premium deck, which contains an astonishing number of cards that go straight into the fully fleshed out Legacy version.

### Elves


The deck good enough in Extended to get [Glimpse of Nature](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glimpse+of+Nature) banned ports over to Legacy easily and with even more toys to play with, most explosively [Gaea's Cradle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gaea%27s+Cradle) and [Priest of Titania](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Priest+of+Titania).


The deck is essentially a creature-based combo deck that generates tons of mana, often unlimited thanks to tricks with [Cloudstone Curio](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cloudstone+Curio), [Nettle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nettle+Sentinel) and [Heritage Druid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Heritage+Druid), and finishes with something like [Ezuri, Renegade Leader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ezuri%2C+Renegade+Leader) or [Mirror Entity](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mirror+Entity).


Caleb Durward didn't utilize the [Cloudstone Curio](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cloudstone+Curio) combo in the list he played to a second place finish at last weekend's SCG Legacy Open, but clearly he didn't need it. Christoffer Anderson even finished third in the same tournament with a similar list.







#### Christoffer Anderson 3rd Star City Legacy Open


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

### Storm


Here we have the rare deck that plays Blue cards but no [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) (usually), even though it does run [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm). ANT  which stands for [Ad Nauseam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ad+Nauseam) Tendrils  is the most common storm deck, and doesn't play [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) in large part because it can't possibly win if it's flipping a five mana spell off of [Ad Nauseam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ad+Nauseam), let alone multiples. Instead the deck leans heavily on cheap discard, such as [Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress), or [Orim's Chant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Orim%27s+Chant) effects to allow it to go off undisturbed. Essentially, the deck is all mana, rituals, tutors and card draw, all of which get chained together in one large turn to make a lethal [Tendrils of Agony](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tendrils+of+Agony). The deck can be built multiple ways, but it almost always takes advantage of [Lion's Eye Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lion%27s+Eye+Diamond) and [Infernal Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Infernal+Tutor), and occasionally packs [Empty the Warrens](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Empty+the+Warrens) as a backup win condition.


### Goblins


Formerly one of the most feared decks in the known universe, Legacy Goblins' [Goblin Lackey](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Lackey) often asked the question "[Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) or no?" on turn one. And if the answer was no, the game was often over right then and there as the deck dumped [Goblin Matron](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Matron)s, Ringleaders and Piledrivers on to the board while disrupting mana bases with [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) and [Rishadan Port](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rishadan+Port).


However, thanks to [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), a rise in [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) thanks to [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets), [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) and a shift to decks like Maverick that can simply block the Lackey (the horror), the deck has fallen by the wayside.


### [Hymn to Tourach](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hymn+to+Tourach) decks


These decks are often hard to categorize and difficult to pin down, but they tend to trade counterspells for discard and the consistency of [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) for the raw power of [Hymn to Tourach](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hymn+to+Tourach).


Popular within the last year, these decks were most often Black and White based for [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant), [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares), [Mother of Runes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mother+of+Runes) and other discard. [Pox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pox) and/or [Smallpox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Smallpox) see some play as well, usually seen alongside [Flagstones of Trokair](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flagstones+of+Trokair) and [Bloodghast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodghast) to mitigate those cards.


There have also been Green versions that used the color for [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), [Pernicious Deed](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pernicious+Deed) and [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary). The fact that some of the BWG decks with Hymn resemble more recent versions of Maverick isn't an accident.


### Lands


One of the coolest, most original decks ever created, Lands (also called 43-Land or some variation thereof) was also at one point one of the best in the format. Though its popularity has waned considerably, it still has its adherents, so don't be surprised to see it pop up here and there this weekend.


Essentially, the deck plays a whole host of specialty lands such as [Maze of Ith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Maze+of+Ith), [Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas), [Mishra's Factory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Factory) and Tabernacle at Pendrell Vale. [Explore](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Explore), [Manabond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Manabond) and [Explore](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Explore) help get multiple lands into play quickly while [Life from the Loam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Life+from+the+Loam) and [Crucible of Worlds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crucible+of+Worlds) keep them coming back for more.


### The rest


As vast as Legacy's card pool is, we can't possibly hope to cover all of the decks, but there are a few that still pop up now and then that are worth mentioning.


Zoo plays all of **Magic**'s best, most efficient beaters with a fetchland heavy mana base. Once one of the most aggressive decks ever, better options in more disruptive or linear shells have passed it by.


Speaking of linear, Affinity decks are still a possibility in Legacy. Every once in a blue moon (but almost never in a [Blood Moon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blood+Moon), which is terrible for the all artifact lands deck to face) the artifact monstrosity puts up a result thanks to its lightning fast starts and powerful cards like [Arcbound Ravager](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arcbound+Ravager) and [Cranial Plating](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cranial+Plating). And with players having ready access to the deck from Modern, don't be surprised to see a few Ravager players spotting the room this weekend.


Beyond those, Enchantress sees play now and then, combining [Argothian Enchantress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Argothian+Enchantress)-like cards with a bevy of enchantments, and White-based Stacks decks that combine artifact mana, [Armageddon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Armageddon) and [Smokestack](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Smokestack) get played by griefers here and there. Aggro Loam, a Jund-based [Life from the Loam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Life+from+the+Loam) deck with [Devastating Dreams](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Devastating+Dreams), sees some play, and Belcher stands as the fastest, if most fragile, combo decks in the format. Belcher  named after it signature card Charbelcher  can win on turn one, but loses to basically any disruption.


Beyond that, there are many, many possible decks we might have missed. Legacy is an incredibly diverse format where just about anything is possible. Stay tuned all weekend to see if a new strategy emerges  possibly around newly unbanned [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax)  or if an old favorite emerges from the pack.




---


**Saturday, 2:01 p.m. - Quick Hits: What effect will [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax) have on the format?**
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Land%20Tax%20Duke.JPG)*Reid Duke  "I think it's a really good card for any fair matchup, but it doesn't help keep combo decks in check. It's a tool."* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Land%20Tax%20Anderson.JPG)*Todd Anderson  "It's not relevant until [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) is banned. Why would you draw three lands when you can draw seven spells?"* 



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Land%20Tax%20Nelson.JPG)*Brad Nelson - "Zero"*

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Land%20Tax%20Black.JPG)*Sam Black - "Minimal."*

**Round 4 Feature Match - Patrick Chapin vs. Korey McDuffie**
-------------------------------------------------------------


*by Steve Sadin*
Pro Tour regular, and Atlanta native Korey McDuffie came into this match beaming with excitement. Why? Because he absolutely loves Legacy.


"Legacy has been my favorite format for a long time. I fell in love with it playing [Standstill](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Standstill) about 5 years ago, and I haven't looked back since."



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/R4%20FM.jpg)

*Patrick Chapin and Korey McDuffie kick off the first feature match of Grand Prix Atlanta* 
His opponent this round, four time Pro Tour Top 8 competitor, Patrick Chapin wasn't quite as excited as the bubbly McDuffie but he was nonetheless very happy with his deck.


### Game One


Chapin won the roll and immediately put his opponent under the gun by casting a turn one [Careful Study](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Careful+Study) discarding [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) and [Animate Dead](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Animate+Dead) (Chapin discarded the two mana reanimation spell because he didn't want to leave himself vulnerable to cards like [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze), [Thalia, Guardian of Thraben](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thalia%2C+Guardian+of+Thraben), [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce), or [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland)).


Chapin's second turn [Reanimate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reanimate) got countered by a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will)  but a [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) (which took [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell), and left McDuffie with a hand of [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand), [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Emrakul%2C+the+Aeons+Torn), and [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will)) allowed Chapin to [Exhume](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Exhume) back his [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) without any resistance.


A few seconds later, McDuffie conceded.


Patrick Chapin 1  Korey McDuffie 0


### Game Two


While game one lasted all of a few turns, the second game went a bit longer, as the players spent their early turns building up their mana (making themselves largely immune to [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze)s, and [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce)s in the process).



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/R4%20FM%20Chapin.JPG)

*Chapin works on building his mana pool* 
McDuffie was the first player to blink, and he was rewarded for doing so, as he was able to push his [Sneak Attack](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sneak+Attack) past Chapin's [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) with a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) of his own.


McDuffie used the [Sneak Attack](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sneak+Attack) to put [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) into play, and promptly drew an extra fourteen cards with it. And while McDuffie didn't find an [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Emrakul%252C%2Bthe%2BAeons%2BTorn), the Aeon's Torn that he could end the game with immediately, he found an abundance of free counterspells to protect him from anything that Chapin could muster.


McDuffie had another [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) a turn later and, after drawing seven more cards with his demon, he found an [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Emrakul%2C+the+Aeons+Torn) to seal the deal.


Patrick Chapin 1  Korey McDuffie 1


### Game Three


A first turn Grafdigger's Cage bought McDuffie a ton of time, giving Chapin no choice but to dig through his deck with [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder), and [Careful Study](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Careful+Study) as he hoped to play enough lands so that he could eventually hard-cast a [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand).



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/R4%20FM%20McDuffie.JPG)

*McDuffie checks his cards to see what his opening move will be.* 
A [Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas) gave Chapin a bit of room to maneuver with, but it ultimately wouldn't be enough. McDuffie had enough countermagic to force through an end of turn [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique) clearing the way for him to resolve a [Sneak Attack](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sneak+Attack) on his own turn.


[Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) was soon to follow, and a [Pithing Needle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pithing+Needle) naming [Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas) allowed McDuffie's [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) to attack unmolested. Another [Sneak Attack](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sneak+Attack)ed [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand), and another attack, later and McDuffie had taken the match.


Patrick Chapin 1  Korey McDuffie 2




---


**Saturday, 4:22 p.m. - Quick Hits: What is the best sideboard card in Legacy?**
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Steve Sadin*

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Levin%20QH.JPG)*Drew Levin  "[Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) in Reanimator since it gives them a way to dodge graveyard hate, and consequently makes it very difficult for other decks to sideboard against them. "* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Kibler%20QH.JPG)*Brian Kibler  "I don't know about the best card, but [Armageddon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Armageddon) is definitely the sweetest card in my sideboard."* 



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Martell%20QH.JPG)*Tom Martell - "[Surgical Extraction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Surgical+Extraction). I think it's the best sideboard card against Reanimator, especially if you're playing [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize)."*
