**Round 5 Feature Match - Brian Braun-Duin vs. Shaheen Soorani**
----------------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
In a 905-person tournament, you expect not to have to play your friends, at least not this early in the tournament when there are metric tons of players with the same records.


Unfortunately for Shaheen Soorani and Brian Braun-Duin, it does happen. The friends and teammates found themselves not only paired against one another in Round 5, but also in a feature match with similar decks.


Soorani was playing Esper Blade with [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls), similar to the deck Tom Martell used to win Grand Prix Columbus a few months back. Braun-Duin was also on Esper Blade, but he did not have the [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) that stood out as Martell's marquee card.


Either way, both players already knew all of that going in. Chatting amicably about their matchup, the configuration of their decks and how their tournament had gone so far, it was certainly the friendliest feature match I've covered in a long time.


### Game 1


Soorani started with a mulligan to 6, one he openly said was less than idea.


"I hope this is the sketchiest 6 ever," Braun-Duin said.


"It's a pretty sketchy 6," Soorani offered.


"But, um, good luck," said Braun-Duin.


Soorani led with an [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) to get a sense of what he was working against, while Braun-Duin used [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) to hide a few cards from his friend's prying eyes.


"I hope I get a [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic)," Soorani said.


"Oh, you'll get a [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic)."


And he definitely did get a [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic), as Braun-Duin revealed a whopping three [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic)s, [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) and two lands.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Round%205%20Soorani.JPG)

*Shaheen Soorani fired off plenty of discard game one, but he quickly found himself behind in the match regardless.* 
Braun-Duin's second Mystic found [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull), but it that was then immediately lost to a [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize).


The players knew each other so well they were bantering back and forth about the proper play, what the odds were of the exact sequence that took place, and even how many of certain cards they had in their decks. It was definitely friendly matchup.


Or at least as friendly as Soorani casting [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) into [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) could be. The third discard spell of the game took a Jitte and revealed [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) and [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique).


A miracle [Terminus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terminus) cleared the board, and Soorani followed up with his own [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic), finding [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull). The equipment didn't get to stay in hand very long as [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique) pushed it to the bottom of Soorani's library.


The Clique and a [Mishra's Factory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Factory) then started Braun-Duin's clock, dropping Soorani to 9 and putting the pressure on tighter.


Soorani tried to stem the bleeding with [Vindicate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vindicate), but [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce) let Braun-Duin keep on churning. When a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) stopped Soorani's attempted [Intuition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intuition), Braun-Duin struck the first blow of the match.


Soorani 0  Braun-Duin 1


### Game 2


"Oh yeah, keeping this one. This is a good one," Soorani said, excited for his seven.


"This is not a good one," a less enthralled Braun-Duin offered. But still he kept.


This time it was Braun-Duin who lead with an [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek), revealing just how saucy Soorani's hand was. Two [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic)s, [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) and three lands stared back at him, and Braun-Duin took one of the Mystics.


The other Mystic searched up [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte) the following turn, but Soorani chose to lead with Vendilion


"You get to see my sweet tech," Braun-Duin said, spreading out a hand of [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel), two [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique)s, [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage), [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) and two Mishra's Factories, with nary a white source to be found. Soorani considered taking nothing, but eventually tucked [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) away.


Braun-Duin then traded his [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique) for Soorani's, tucking a [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor) as the two faeries fell to the Legend rule.


Meanwhile, Jitte entered the battlefield and came in at Braun-Duin attached to the [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic).



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Round%205%20Braun-Duin.JPG)

*Brian Braun-Duin has typically gotten the best of Soorani, and Round 5 looked like it might not be any different.* 
A second [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique) from Braun-Duin buried Soorani's remaining [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls), but it also quickly jumped in front of the Jitte-wielding [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic).


[Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) dispatched the Mystic, but Soorani fired back with a [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) on [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) and a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) on [Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas), once again cutting Braun-Duin off from white mana. Soorani finished his big turn with another [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) for [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull). He even drew [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) the following turn, putting his friend even further behind.


When a [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) revealed nothing of use, Braun-Duin conceded to a massive board disadvantage.


Soorani 1  Braun-Duin 1


### Game 3


Braun-Duin had the first action of the final game, using a [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) to search up [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) while Soorani [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)ed twice to find land...and missed both times.


"That would be game over, I think," Soorani said, discarding on his second turn.


Soorani's third [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) did find a land, finally, and enabled him to [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) Braun-Duin, who [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)ed in response. Once [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) resolved, Braun-Duin revealed a hand with no legal targets for the [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Inquisition%2Bof%2BKozilek), "just" a [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) and [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor).



![Batterskull++Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Batterskull&options=)
![Batterskull++Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Jace,%20the%20Mind%20Sculptor&options=)

Facing two cards his hand couldn't handle, Soorani was quick to pack it in.


"You keep getting me," Soorani said.


"I do. And I keep feeling like I'm lucky to do so."


Soorani 1  Braun-Duin 1




---


**Saturday, 5:19 p.m. - [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand): Why 7 > 3.**
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
While talking to players this morning about the unbanning of [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax), a common theme kept coming out of their answers.


Why would you draw three lands when you can draw seven spells?


Todd Anderson delivered that particular gem of a quote, but the sentiment was the same from pretty much everyone. Seven > three, so why not draw more?


The seven everyone is referring to is the new bad boy of the giant creatures catalogue, [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand). The *Avacyn Restored* Demon has become the de facto creature to cheat into play with [Reanimate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reanimate), [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell), [Sneak Attack](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sneak+Attack) and others thanks to one of the most powerful lines of text in **Magic**: Draw seven.



![Griselbrand++Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Griselbrand&options=)
![Griselbrand++Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Land%20Tax&options=)

*7 > 3*
Among [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand)'s most fervent supporters is Gerry Thompson, who thinks the Legendary Demon is simply the best thing to do in Legacy.


"Legacy is all about tempo and 1-for-1ing your opponent. It's too fast for mass card draw. [Fact or Fiction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fact+or+Fiction), [Ancestral Vision](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancestral+Vision), those are all legal, but are too slow," Thompson said. "[Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) isn't."


A number of other pros and joes agree. Much of the Channelfireball crew is on [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) decks, and a general sweep of the tournament floor reveals [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) after [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) after [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) (one of which was hilariously being held in check by [Elephant Grass](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elephant+Grass) when I walked by).


The difference is that [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand), once in play, isn't tempo negative like a [Fact or Fiction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fact+or+Fiction) would be. The 7/7 lifelinker is a scary board presence in addition to being a draw engine, meaning that you won't get accidentally run over while resolving your draw spell.


In fact, Thompson said [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) translates into a win for Reanimator more often than not, something he said it hasn't had before. [Iona, Shield of Emeria](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Iona%2C+Shield+of+Emeria) could be attacked from a number of angles, [Blazing Archon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blazing+Archon) and [Elesh Norn, Grand Cenobite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elesh+Norn%2C+Grand+Cenobite) are unimpressive against many decks, and [Terastodon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terastodon) often doesn't do enough. There was only card Thompson saw as even a close corollary.


"Jin-Gitaxis does the same thing, but it dies to too many cards," Thompson said.


It's also significantly worse against one of the breakout cards of the weekend, [Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas). Dealers have reported strong interest in the Legendary and Legend-bouncing land. Once primarily a combo with [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique) and a way to keep [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Emrakul%252C%2Bthe%2BAeons%2BTorn), the Aeon's Torn off your back, [Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas) has emerged as a way to keep [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) from gaining any of the life back.


In fact, Thompson lost a round today to an Zoo deck sporting cards such as [Crop Rotation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crop+Rotation) to ensure they find [Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas).


So far, we've concentrated mostly on bringing [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) back from the graveyard, but Reanimator isn't the only deck to take advantage of the *Avacyn Restored* All-Star. Sneak and Show  a deck built around [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) and [Sneak Attack](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sneak+Attack)  also regards [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) highly.


When [Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas) isn't involved, [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Emrakul%252C%2Bthe%2BAeons%2BTorn), the Aeon's Torn is sometimes a better creature to sneak into play, often translating directly into a win or, at the very least, an empty board. But no Sneak and Show player is going to complain when they have to "settle" for [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand). On the other hand, sneaking in [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) and immediately drawing seven can mean that the Sneak and Show player finds an [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Emrakul%252C%2Bthe%2BAeons%2BTorn) to sneak in alongside his new best friend.



![Griselbrand++Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Griselbrand&options=)
![Griselbrand++Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Emrakul,%20the%20Aeons%20Torn&options=)

*BFF, or at least until one of them is banned.*
The power of [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) hasn't just increased the importance of [Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas), it has also increased the importance of having a clock.


Thompson said that slow decks with disruption allowed [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) decks to shape their hand and even draw seven without getting in an attack, but disruptive decks that can attack  like hateful Zoo builds and normal Merfolk  can cause problems for the deck. If the [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) player can't afford to draw seven until it gets an attack in, it leaves it vulnerable to all kinds of plays.


For instance, Thompson said there really was no good answer for [ther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=%C3%86ther+Vial) plus [Phantasmal Image](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantasmal+Image). Even this weekend's super techy Not of this World can't save [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) from a [Phantasmal Image](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantasmal+Image).



![Not of this World](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Not+of+this+World)

Despite the power of Avacyn's nemesis, not everyone was enthralled by its presence this weekend.


Reid Duke was one of the people responsible for Reanimator's resurgence when he won the Star City Games Legacy Open on June 10 with [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) Reanimator, yet this weekend he's skipped the deck in favor of a more controlling deck.


"I played with it before people were expecting it and after people were expecting it, and it was a very different experience," he said.


When he won the tournament, Duke said all of his games were close, but he won. The next week, when it was more known, he said all of his games were close, but with the opposite result.


"It definitely felt like one to two sideboard cards made the difference," he said.


Duke added that he expected a ton of people to play [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) in Atlanta this weekend, but that even then he underestimated its popularity




---


**Round 6 Feature Match - Owen Turtenwald vs. Drew Levin**
----------------------------------------------------------


*by Steve Sadin*

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/R6%20FM.JPG)

*Two undefeated Black-Blue Reanimator decks square off, only one will win.* 
After five rounds reigning Player of the Year Owen Turtenwald, and Legacy specialist Drew Levin both found themselves with undefeated records. Their weapons of choice? Two extremely similar Black-Blue Reanimator decks.


### Game One


Levin won the roll and opened with a first turn [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) revealing a hand of two [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize)s, a [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), an [Entomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Entomb), and a couple of lands. Drew took a [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize), but he could do nothing to prevent Owen from resolving his own discard spell a few seconds later.


Owen's [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) revealed a hand of [Careful Study](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Careful+Study), [Animate Dead](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Animate+Dead), [Elesh Norn, Grand Cenobite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elesh+Norn%2C+Grand+Cenobite), [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize), and [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder)  Turtenwald (who had just drawn a [Reanimate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reanimate) to go with his [Entomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Entomb)) opted to take a [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) in turn.


Levin untapped and cast a [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder), keeping the top three cards, but nonetheless passed his turn without a second land. Turtenwald then played a land and passed his turn before casting a [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), and an [Entomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Entomb) at the end of Levin's turn.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/R6%20FM%20Levin.JPG)

*Levin takes the first game* 
Owen attempted to go for the kill by using a [Reanimate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reanimate) to bring back his [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) -- but Drew had a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) to counter [Reanimate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reanimate), and a [Reanimate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reanimate) of his own to grab the [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) out of Turtenwald's graveyard.


A couple of turns, and about 14 extra cards later, and Levin was up a game.


Drew Levin 1  Owen Turtenwald 0


### Game Two


While the first game was over in a matter of turns, the second game dragged on a bit longer as the players were content to spend their early turns playing lands, and sculpting their hands with [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)s, and [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder)s.


Drew blinked first by casting an end of turn [Entomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Entomb)  but Drew didn't search for a [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand)  instead he found a [Coffin Purge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Coffin+Purge). This [Coffin Purge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Coffin+Purge), along with the [Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas) that he already had in play, gave Levin quite a bit of protection from any reanimation plans that Turtenwald might have.


However, Turtenwald wasn't trying to reanimate anything  a fact that he quickly demonstrated as his end of turn [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique) cleared the way for a [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor).


Levin's [Entomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Entomb) found him a [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand), but his attempt to [Reanimate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reanimate) it was met with [Coffin Purge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Coffin+Purge). The players traded [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will)s, and Levin was finally able sneak a [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) into play thanks to a second [Entomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Entomb), and a second [Reanimate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reanimate).



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/R6FM%20Jace%20vs%20Griselbrand.JPG)

*[Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) ain't got nothing on Jace* 
Levin drew a bunch of extra cards with his [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand), but with no way to keep a threat in play through [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor) for more than a turn it wasn't long before Levin conceded.


Drew Levin 1  Owen Turtenwald 1


### Game Three


Levin had a lightning fast draw for the third game, using an [Entomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Entomb) to search for a [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand), an [Animate Dead](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Animate+Dead), and a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) to protect his [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) from [Coffin Purge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Coffin+Purge)...



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/R6%20FM%20Owen.JPG)

*Turtenwald's [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) uses Levin's own [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) against him to continue undefeated.* 
However, Turtenwald had a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) of his own to counter his opponent's reanimation spell -- as well as an [Animate Dead](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Animate+Dead) which he used to bring his opponent's demon into play under his own control, and take the third game in the matter of minutes.


Owen Turtenwald 2  Drew Levin 1




---


**Round 7 Feature Match - Ian Duke vs. Sam Black**
--------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
I really could not be more excited for this matchup, and it has nothing to do with the players sitting across from one another.


Don't get me wrong, I'm a big fan of Sam Black, ever since he beat me in Regionals about 8 years ago with a deck that could best be described as "unique." Since then, he's gone on to accomplish just about everything under the sun, including Pro Tour Top 8s and representing team USA.


His opponent this round is Ian Duke, a player short on Black's resume, but long on family connections. The brother of All-World All-Star Reid Duke, Ian Duke was 5-1 coming into the round and was sporting the same deck his brother was piloting, a UW Miracles control deck.


Still, it was their decks that gave me all kinds of chills when I saw the pairings. The Duke family deck is a UW Miracles deck that packs the newly unbanned [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax) and several very cool ways to get value out of it. Plus, ya know,  *[Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax)*.


Black, meanwhile, might be piloting the most unique deck at the tournament. It is a Red-Black-White zombies, [Goblin Bombardment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Bombardment), [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls), [Carrion Feeder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Carrion+Feeder), [Blood Artist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blood+Artist), [Bitterblossom](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bitterblossom), [Faithless Looting](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Faithless+Looting), *thing*. That's really the best way I can describe it. He, too, was 5-1.


I mean, [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax) versus [Goblin Bombardment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Bombardment)? What year is it again?


### Game 1


A turn one [Relic of Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Relic+of+Progenitus) looked pretty good against a deck packing [Bloodghast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodghast), [Faithless Looting](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Faithless+Looting) and [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler), but the really interesting card came on turn two when Duke played [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax).


"Ooooohhhh," cooed Black when he saw the *Legends* enchantment. Not many people had brought the recently unbanned card this weekend, and Black, like myself, seemed intrigued to see it on the table.


Not too be outdone, Black had a pretty oohh-worth plan of his own. He led with a turn one [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler), followed by [Faithless Looting](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Faithless+Looting) into a second [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler) jumping out of the graveyard.


Then Duke did something awesome. He popped a fetchland on Black's turn, but "failed to find" any land. That let him trigger his [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax) on his turn.


"Very tricky," said Black, who had played his second land.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Round%207%20Ian%20Duke.JPG)

*Ian Duke has spent a lot of time [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax)ing this weekend, making him pretty adept at searching his library.* 
[Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) took care of one [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler) as [Relic of Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Relic+of+Progenitus) ate away at Black's graveyard. Suddenly, his start didn't look quite as hot, especially as he was forced to play a third land right into [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax).


[Tidehollow Sculler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tidehollow+Sculler) met [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), and Duke made up the card disadvantage with another turn of [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax).


A second Sculler landed, but revealed a hand of seven lands, flush from [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax). Looking for action, Duke used his Relic to draw a card, eventually finding [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) on his turn.


It was, however, a blind [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) without much backup. He would need to find some extra action to keep up.


Duke missed on the [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) trigger when Black played [Blood Artist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blood+Artist), testing the waters. The flip revealed a [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor), meaning Black could more safely resolve the [Goblin Bombardment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Bombardment) waiting in his hand.


However, Duke shuffled off a fetchland in response to the Bombardment and blind flipped again, this time hitting [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze). It let him live, but wasn't a particularly helpful card to draw the following turn.


After another turn of attacks dropped him to just three life, [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor) gave Duke something of a lease on life, keeping him alive for one more turn...or so he thought. Black found a [Carrion Feeder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Carrion+Feeder) and was able to drain Duke out from three with [Blood Artist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blood+Artist).


Black 1  Duke 0


### Game 2


Once again Duke led with an early [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax).


So what does Black do?



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Land%20Tax%20Go.JPG)

*What do you do? What do you do?!* 
"Move to discard?"


Of course, the card he discarded was [Bloodghast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodghast), which popped right back into play the following turn. Black attempted to play [Carrion Feeder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Carrion+Feeder) for [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) protection, but Duke had the Swords to remove the [Bloodghast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodghast) first.


[Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) named [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze), and missed, but did reveal a whopping three [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor), [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) and [Entreat the Angels](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Entreat+the+Angels).


"This game is not going so well for me," Duke said.


[Carrion Feeder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Carrion+Feeder) continued attacking, while Black cast and resolved [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant)...


...right before Duke cast a miracle [Terminus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terminus).


The players continued their back and forth as a [Bitterblossom](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bitterblossom) was [Disenchant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Disenchant)ed, only to be replaced by a second [Bitterblossom](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bitterblossom) and [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls).


The first Faerie token was sacrificed to [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) to pitch all three [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor)s, revealing two [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) and [Entreat the Angels](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Entreat+the+Angels). Things had quickly turned sour for Duke, even after he finally found a second [Tundra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tundra), enabling [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance).



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Round%207%20Black.JPG)

*Sam Black just might be sporting the most unique deck of the weekend.* 
The [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) missed the next turn when Black cast [Goblin Bombardment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Bombardment), a card which was especially deadly with the swarm of tokens he was amassing and the [Bloodghast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodghast) he followed up with.


By the time Black hit six tokens, Duke could only manage to Entreat some Angels. However, thanks to [Goblin Bombardment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Bombardment), even with a few angels in play, Duke was dead on board.


Black 2  Duke 0




---


**Saturday, 6:50 p.m. - Key Sideboard cards in Legacy**
-------------------------------------------------------


*by Steve Sadin*
Sometimes players will go through an entire Booster Draft without so much as touching their sideboard  and that's perfectly okay. If you were struggling to get enough playable cards, then you might not have anything worth sideboarding in.


But in a format like Legacy, where players can kill you on turn one with a [Goblin Charbelcher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Charbelcher), attack with an [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Emrakul%2C+the+Aeons+Torn) on turn two, or simply build up a strong board with cards like [Mother of Runes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mother+of+Runes), and [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary) while keeping you off of your spells with [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland)s, you better come prepared with a good sideboard.


Not sure what to put in your Legacy sideboard? Well, then you should probably keep reading!



![Meekstone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Meekstone)

RUG [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets)'s creatures are big, and they're cheap. But the fact that all of their creatures are big isn't always a good thing... For a mere one mana, [Meekstone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Meekstone) affects every one of RUG [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets)'s creatures, ensuring that they can only attack once before they're locked down forever.


Can a RUG [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets) deck beat a resolved [Meekstone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Meekstone) without destroying it? Yes, it technically can, but that's going to be a serious uphill battle.


So if you're playing a deck that doesn't need big creatures to win, and you find yourself having trouble with RUG [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets) decks  then you should probably look to stick a couple of [Meekstone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Meekstone)s in your sideboard. You won't be disappointed.



![Mind Harness](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Mind+Harness)

While very few cards are as potent as [Meekstone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Meekstone) against RUG [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets), if you're playing a deck full of 3+ power creatures then it's going to be difficult for you to make good use of the one mana artifact. So if you find that you need to look elsewhere for cards to strengthen your RUG [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets) matchup, then you should take a close look at [Mind Harness](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mind+Harness).


While [Mind Harness](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mind+Harness) might not be able to take a [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose)  if you use it to snatch a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), or Scavenging Ooze, it probably won't take long for you to cruise to victory.


Additionally, [Mind Harness](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mind+Harness) can take [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary) from Maverick decks, and [Priest of Titania](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Priest+of+Titania)s (as well as just about any other combo piece that you might want to grab) from Elf decks.



![Submerge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Submerge)

Alright, maybe [Mind Harness](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mind+Harness) isn't a good fit for your deck either because you can't reliably kill your opponent before you run out of mana to pay the cumulative upkeep on [Mind Harness](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mind+Harness). In that case, you should look no further than [Submerge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Submerge) to help you with your green creature problems.


### Graveyard Hate


Between [Faerie Macabre](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Faerie+Macabre), [Coffin Purge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Coffin+Purge), Tormnod's Crypt, [Relic of Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Relic+of+Progenitus), Grafdigger's Cage, [Bojuka Bog](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bojuka+Bog), and [Leyline of the Void](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Leyline+of+the+Void), [Extirpate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Extirpate), [Surgical Extraction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Surgical+Extraction), (to name a few), there are a lot of good anti-graveyard cards to choose from  and if you're playing in a Legacy tournament any time soon, you better have some of them in your sideboard.


If you don't put any graveyard hate in your sideboard, then don't be surprised if you find yourself taking a lot of losses at the hands of reanimated [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand)s, and armies of [Bridge from Below](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bridge+from+Below) tokens.



![Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Show+and+Tell)

When asked to name the best sideboard card in Legacy, Drew Levin immediately identified [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) out of Reanimator's sideboard. Drew thinks that [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) stands head and shoulders above the competition "since it gives them a way to dodge graveyard hate, and consequently makes it very difficult for other decks to sideboard against them."


So if you're playing Reanimator, you better make sure that you've got a set of [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell)s (and potentially some more lands to help you cast them) in your sideboard. And if you're playing against Reanimator, then you better be ready for your opponents to spend three mana to put a [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) into play directly from their hand.



![Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor)

[Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) isn't the only card that Reanimator players can sideboard in to give their strategy a serious overhaul. Not by a long shot.


[Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor) gives Reanimator decks another angle of attack that doesn't require them to touch their graveyards, or give their opponents the opportunity to put the biggest threat in their hand into play for free.


Between [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor)  and [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique), Reanimator decks can play through entire games like a traditional control deck... albeit one that's capable of sneaking a game dominating [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) into play as early as turn two should their opponent let their guard down.



![Ancient Grudge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Ancient+Grudge)

While there might not be a ton of artifacts running around in Legacy right now  it's rarely bad to fit an [Ancient Grudge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancient+Grudge) or two into your sideboard if you need some help dealing with [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull)s, and Umezawa's Jittes.



![Sylvan Library](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Sylvan+Library)

Looking for a tool that will allow you to outlast control decks, and help you dig for your hate cards against combo decks? Then look no further than [Sylvan Library](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvan+Library).


While you might not want to pay any life to draw extra cards against a Mono-Red Burn deck  if you're playing against a deck that has no good way to apply pressure to you before they've completely taken over the game, then there's no reason why you can't pay 12, or even 16 extra life to draw a bunch of extra cards.


### Other good options


Still looking for some more good cards for your sideboard? Well [Pyroblast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pyroblast), [Hydroblast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hydroblast), [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance), [Gilded Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gilded+Drake), [Leyline of Sanctity](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Leyline+of+Sanctity), [Engineered Plague](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Engineered+Plague), [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte), [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce), and [Spell Snare](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Snare) all come to mind as potent options depending on what you're trying to accomplish. And beyond that, there are thousands of other cards just waiting for their chance to shine in your Legacy sideboard.


You just need to find the right job for them.




---


**Saturday, 6:53 p.m. - Land Tax, a Short History**
---------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
In the run up to the June 20 banned and restricted announcement, much of the fervor and anticipation surrounded the fate of the Standard [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets) deck. But when no changes were made the Standard list, attention turned to the one change that was made.


### Legacy


[Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax) is Unbanned



![Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Land+Tax)

Three little words could make a world of difference this weekend. One of the most powerful enchantments ever printed, [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax) has been banned in Legacy since 2004 and has at times been one of the most dominant spells in the game.


Probably the best known [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax) deck was Randy Buehler's Tax Rack deck that abused the synergy between [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax) and [Scroll Rack](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scroll+Rack) to turn [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax)'s one "disadvantage" (if you can call it that) of searching up only basic lands into a virtual [Ancestral Recall](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancestral+Recall) every turn.


Buehler won the North American Extended Championship in 1998 with this beauty.







#### Randy Buehler


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

##### Rare (21)

4
[Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BLand%5D+%5BTax%5D)


3
[Scroll Rack](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BScroll%5D+%5BRack%5D)


4
[Tithe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BTithe%5D)


2
[Suleiman's Legacy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BSuleiman%5D+%5BLegacy%5D)



##### Mythic (8)



4
[Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BWasteland%5D)


4
[Mox Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BMox%5D+%5BDiamond%5D)


75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Kjeldoran+Outpost)


















While we're a little bit past the point of [Sand Golem](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sand+Golem) and [Suleiman's Legacy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Suleiman%27s+Legacy) being viable cards, the [Scroll Rack](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scroll+Rack) + [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax) synergy is still incredibly powerful and is probably the first place to start when looking at the enchantment's viability in modern Legacy.



![Scroll Rack](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Scroll+Rack)

However, [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax), originally printed in *Legends*, has a history that goes back to the very beginnings of the Pro Tour.


Though we don't have all of the deck lists from the 1995 World Championship, we can say for sure that the finals came down to two decks that both sported the white enchantment.







#### Alexander Blumke


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

77 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Adarkar+Wastes)


















And, yes, the decks had 63 and 62 cards in the main deck. What can I say, times were different back then.


So different that decks that sported [Zuran Orb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zuran+Orb) and [Armageddon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Armageddon) did not play the full four [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax) (it was not yet restricted). Yet you can see the seeds of how the enchantment would be later abused. [Zuran Orb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zuran+Orb) let players manipulate the number of lands in play, [Ivory Tower](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ivory+Tower) makes use of all the extra cards in hand, and [Armageddon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Armageddon) puts players in a pinch as to exactly what they need to play around.


[Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax) made its name known in Standard (then called Type II) around 1996 when [Black Vise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Black+Vise) was restricted. Bertrand Lestree of France took 2nd at Pro Tour New York in 1996 with Ernhamgeddon, a deck with was based around getting out a quick [Erhnam Djinn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Erhnam+Djinn) (then the premier fatty of its day) and follow it up with an [Armageddon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Armageddon) and artifact or creature mana.

75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Brushland)


















Again note the use of [Zuran Orb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zuran+Orb) and [Ivory Tower](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ivory+Tower) (then both restricted) as well as [Armageddon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Armageddon). Notice that there was even [Sylvan Library](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvan+Library) to give a look and shuffle effect with [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax), something of a precursor to fetchlands plus [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) or [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top), if a bit of an awkward one.


At this point, [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax) was fighting with [Necropotence](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Necropotence) for space in the top decks. Ernhamgeddon was something of a foil to Necro decks (notice Lestree's main deck [Order of Leitbur](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Order+of+Leitbur)). After all, it doesn't matter how many cards you draw if you have no lands in play.


Speaking of anti-Necro decks, [Stasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stasis) was a similarly popular strategy for fighting the Necro menace, and Matt Place took Turbo [Stasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stasis) to the Top 8 of U.S. Nationals in 1996.







#### Matt Place


#####

![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Adarkar+Wastes)


















But, as many who played during that period know, [Necropotence](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Necropotence) was the clear winner in that race. During what became known as the "Black Summer," [Necropotence](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Necropotence) dominated the tournament scene, overshadowing [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax) and, well, everything else as well.


[Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax) would again have its day in the sun in Extended with Buehler's Tax Rack deck as well as from a then little-known player named John Finkel, who won Grand Prix Rio de Janeiro in 1998 with a more aggressive version based around [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax) and [Empyrial Armor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Empyrial+Armor). (Note: The sideboard is lost to the ravages of time.)
