60 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Plains)


















Fast forward to 2004 and the creation of Legacy. By that time, [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax) had earned its fearsome reputation as a card to be frightened of. What's more, it led to some fairly uninteresting games of **Magic**, where both players would simply refuse to play lands, staring at one another until someone blinked.


As a result, [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax) was added to the Legacy banned list at the outset of the format, never to see play...


...until now.


So far, opinions from pros have been [fairly negative](http://www.wizards.com/Magic/Magazine/Article.aspx?x=mtg/daily/eventcoverage/gpatl12/welcome#2), but at least one notable pro is playing it this weekend.


Oddly enough, the reason most players think [Land Tax](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Tax) won't break out this weekend is that it will be overshadowed by [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand), another black spell that trades life 1-for-1 to draw cards.



![Necropotence++Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Necropotence&options=)
![Necropotence++Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Griselbrand&options=)

*The more things change, the more they stay the same.*


---


**Saturday, 8:11 p.m. - Photo Essay: Legacy is Kind of Awesome, pt. 1**
-----------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
As the most played eternal format, Legacy offers so many different viable decks it can make your head spin a little bit. Goblins and [Grindstone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grindstone)s and Elves and Reanimators and [Metalworker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Metalworker)s and Stoneforges and 87 flavors of [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets) and more.


This is a format where [Goblin Welder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Welder), one of the best one drops of all time, is scarcely played at all. It's a format where Elves is a combo deck and where the mightiest [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand)s get stuck in the slightest bit of [Elephant Grass](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elephant+Grass). And it's a format where sometimes a turn two [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Emrakul%2C+the+Aeons+Torn) just isn't enough.


Basically, it's kind of awesome.


All day we've been gathering pictures of unusual, entertaining, odd or just plain interesting game states from tables up and down the tournament hall. Every one of these actually happened in the main tournament, and most of them were so cool we just couldn't pass up a photo.


So, from my camera to your computer, here are some of the just plain coolest things to happen this weekend.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Kobolds.JPG)

*Here there be 18/19 Kobolds.* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Elephant%20Grass.JPG)

*Maybe his hooks get stuck in the grass? The [Elephant Grass](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elephant+Grass), that is.* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Humiliating.JPG)

*You know whats Humiliating? This!* 

![Humility](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Humility)


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Orb%20Tax.JPG)

*Fun fact: three of these four cards have been banned or restricted in some format at some time...* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Bombardment.JPG)

*[Goblin Bombardment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Bombardment)?! (Not shown: His opponent's life total. Because he's dead.)* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Baneslayer.JPG)

*Protection from Demons you say?* 


---


**Round 8 Feature Match - Alexander Hayne vs. David Shiels**
------------------------------------------------------------


*by Steve Sadin*
A few minutes after his grueling match against Pro Tour *Avacyn Restored* finalist Gaudenis Vidugiris ended in an unintentional draw, Grand Prix Dallas champion David Shiels now has to face the one man who was able to outlast Gaudenis at Pro Tour *Avacyn Restored*  the champion Alexander Hayne.


### Game One


Hayne won the roll and immediately put the pressure on with a pair of [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets), and a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) on Shiels' only land. However, Shiels was quick to capitalize on the situation by using a [Forked Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forked+Bolt) to take out both of Hayne's creatures.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/R8%20FM.JPG)

*Alexander Hayne and David Shiels square off* 
Hayne rebuilt with a [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose), but Shiels was again able to neutralize the situation by using a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) to take out Hayne's only green source before playing a [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose) of his own. The mongooses traded, and when Hayne passed the turn without a follow-up play Shiels decided that it was time to hop into the driver's seat by casting a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf).


However, David's attempts to go on the offensive would ultimately prove to be about as successful as Alex's early tries  as his first [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) got countered, and his second died at the hands of a [Dismember](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dismember).



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/R8%20FM%20Shiels.JPG)

*David Shiels attempts to mount an offense come to naught* 
At this point, Shiels found himself without any threats left, and once again had to spend his time reacting. First he used a [Dismember](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dismember) to take out a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), then, when Hayne played an untargettable [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose) he began digging rapidly to find a [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose) of his own which he could trade with.


[Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) allowed Hayne to recoup some of the card advantage that he had lost over the course of the game  however, a [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt), and a couple of [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze)s ensured that it wouldn't have any immediate impact.


A couple of turns later, Shiels found a new threat. But rather than jump out of his seat and immediately cast the spell, Shiels used a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) to knock Hayne down to four lands before trying his [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose). With only four lands, Hayne had no choice but to [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) the [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose) by exiling the only other remaining card in his hand  a second [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will).



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/R8%20FM%20Hayne.JPG)

*Alexander Hayne battles valiantly, however falls to Shiels' [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf)*
And that would ultimately be the last relevant play that Hayne made. Because after their grueling war of attrition had gone on for nearly 30 minutes, Shiels was finally able to resolve a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) which he rode to victory.


Dave Shiels 1  Alexander Hayne 0


### Game Two


Hayne opened on [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets), while Shiels wasted no time before [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland)ing Hayne's [Volcanic Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Volcanic+Island). That play began paying dividends to Shiels immediately as Hayne had no land to replace it with.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/R8%20FM%20final%20picture.JPG)

*Shiels' kept Hayne mana-less for the majority of the second game* 
And by the time Hayne found his second land, Shiels was ready with a second [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland), and a [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce) to counter Hayne's [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm).


It was a long time until Hayne finally found a land that he could keep, and at that point it was too late as Shiels had a [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose), a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), and an [Insectile Aberration](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Insectile+Aberration) to swing to victory with.


David Shiels 2  Alexander Hayne 0




---


**Round 9 Feature Match - Ali Aintrazi vs. Jesse Hatfield**
-----------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
Both Ali Aintrazi and Jesse Hatfield were safely on their way to Day 2 at this point, sporting nearly pristine 7-1 records with just one round to go before the cut. But any time you can feature a Hatfield against a former U.S. national champion, you've got to do it.


Jesse Hatfield was one half of the famous Hatfield brothers who had made [High Tide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=High+Tide) a deck to beat for some time last year and put [Candelabra of Tawnos](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Candelabra+of+Tawnos) back on the map. Hatfield wasn't playing the mono Blue monstrosity this weekend, but was instead battling with a BUG [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets) deck that dipped into [Temporal Mastery](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Temporal+Mastery) to really break [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) and [Sylvan Library](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvan+Library) in half.


Aintrazi had some spicy cards himself. Playing Esper Stoneblade, Aintrazi was also packing [Humility](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Humility), which made his [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) even more effective and his equipment dominant. But Hatfield's deck was even more tempo oriented than most, meaning resolving a four-mana enchantment could prove troublesome.


### Game 1


A mulligan to six put Hatfield behind to begin, and Aintrazi's [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) put him even further back. The discard spell revealed two [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets), two [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) and a [Sylvan Library](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvan+Library) to go with a land. One of the [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets)s fell to [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Inquisition%2Bof%2BKozilek), but the other entered play on Hatfield's first turn.



![Delver of Secret](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Delver+of+Secret)

[Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets) didn't flip, but Hatfield had to [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) for a second land, and even then it was a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) rather than colored mana.


Aintrazi's [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) rebought [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek), revealing [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) and yet another [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets). Aintrazi chose the 'Goyf and passed the turn, clearing the way for Hatfield to resolve the [Sylvan Library](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvan+Library) he had hidden at the top of his library.


[Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) flipped the [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets) the following turn, and Hatfield paid eight life to draw all of the cards off of his [Sylvan Library](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvan+Library) before [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder)ing.


But when [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets) attacked, Aintrazi attempted to ambush it with [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique). [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze) kept it from entering play, and Hatfield cast his previously revealed [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets), hoping to steal the match through the air.


The air was exactly where Aintrazi was prepared to fight once he resolved [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls).


Hatfield's draw step, however, yielded the [Temporal Mastery](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Temporal+Mastery) he had stacked on top. He cast the miracle [Time Walk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Walk) and attacked his [Insectile Aberration](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Insectile+Aberration)s into Aintrazi's [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) tokens, losing one but taking Aintrazi to 11 in the process.



![Temporal Mastery](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Temporal+Mastery)

A second miracled [Temporal Mastery](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Temporal+Mastery) kept Hatfield chaining turns together and getting in damage with the Aberration, dropping Aintrazi to five life.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Round%209%20Aintrazi.JPG)

*Here you see Ali Aintrazi not taking any turns in Game 1.* 
More cantrips, more shuffling and more deck manipulation let Hatfield continually stack his deck until he was satisfied. Eventually, he gave Aintrazi a turn, which was used to simply flash back [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls).


But a third [Temporal Mastery](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Temporal+Mastery) yielded yet another extra turn. During his first turn, Hatfield made a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf). On his second, Hatfield's attacked Aintrazi to just one life after some [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) chump blocking. Hatfield finished by [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland)ing one of Aintrazi's two white sources, stranding a [Humility](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Humility) in his hand.


Aintrazi drew a [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) to give him a shot, but [Sylvan Library](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvan+Library) turned up [Ghastly Demise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ghastly+Demise), clearing the way for Hatfield to deliver the lethal blow.


Hatfield 1  Aintrazi 0


### Game 2


Hatfield's first attempt to manipulate his deck  [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder)  was [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce)d, followed by Aintrazi Surgically Extracting all of Hatfield's copies of the blue sorcery.


No copies were trapped in his hand, but it did reveal two [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland), [Tropical Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tropical+Island), a [Sylvan Library](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvan+Library), [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize), [Engineered Explosives](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Engineered+Explosives) and a [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets).


One of the [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland)s hit Aintrazi's [Tundra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tundra), prompting a [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) before the anticipated [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize). Instead, Hatfield ran [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets) onto the board.


The [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets) flipped the next turn on a revealed [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), but before Hatfield could add it to his hand, Aintrazi used [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) to flash back [Surgical Extraction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Surgical+Extraction), hitting Hatfield's other [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) sitting in his hand and shuffling away the [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm). Hatfield didn't miss a beat, though, casting the [Sylvan Library](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvan+Library) that had been so key last game.


Meanwhile, Aintrazi shot back with his own dangerous two drop, casting [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte) to go with his [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage).


A [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) from Hatfield took [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage), leaving Aintrazi with just a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) in hand, but a ready Jitte.


[Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) traded with [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets) on Aintrazi's attack, depriving him of a creature, but giving him two potentially important Jitte counters.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Round%209%20Hatfield.JPG)

*And here we see Jesse Hatfield taking practically all the turns in Game 2. Seemed fair.* 
The board now clear of threats, Hatfield started milking his [Sylvan Library](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvan+Library). First he miracled [Temporal Mastery](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Temporal+Mastery) for an extra turn, then he paid four life to draw an extra card off the library. He used his extra turn to cast and resolve a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), and Aintrazi had no response. The former U.S. champ's hand still two blanks, meaning he had to watch the next turn as well as [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets) joined Hatfield's growing board presence.


A [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic), though, gave him a ray of hope. He found a [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull), equipped his Jitte to the Mystic and passed the turn. With just seven life, Aintrazi's margin of error was slim at best. He used one Jitte counter to kill the [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets) before it flipped, but his odds only got worse when Hatfield miracled another [Temporal Mastery](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Temporal+Mastery).


[Ghastly Demise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ghastly+Demise) cleared out the Mystic, and an Engineered Exposives for zero left Aintrazi with no outs.


Hatfield 2  Aintrazi 0




---


**Saturday, 10:05 p.m. - Round 9 Roundup: Bobbling all around the Bubble**
--------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Steve Sadin*
While Ben Stark, and Alex Hon were busy running the tables on Day One, quite a few other players entered the final round of the day with 6-2 records, and in need of a win to be able to play tomorrow. Lest we ignore these players who were busy fighting for their tournament lives, I decided to check in on some of them and report on the results.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/R9%20Roundup%20Kibler.JPG)

*Table 50 Brian Kibler vs. Kevin Bopp* 
When Kevin Bopp reanimated a [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) into play on turn two, things looked bad for Brian Kibler. When Kevin connected with his [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) twice, and drew a ton of extra cards, it looked like Kevin was well on his way to Day Two...


But just before that happened, Kibler drew the [Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas) that he needed to get himself right back into the game  allowing Kibler to overcome the odds, and advance to Day Two.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/R9%20Roundup%20David%20Ochoa.JPG)

*Table 66 David Ochoa vs. Greg Mitchell* 
After splitting the first two games, David Ochoa was unable to find a way to put a [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) into his Reanimator deck's graveyard in the deciding game. So instead, he decided to reanimate the [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary) that was sitting in Greg Mitchell's graveyard.


Greg did what he could to make a game of it, but he ultimately succumbed beneath the weight of [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor) and his own undead [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary).



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/R9%20Roundup%20Laluge%20vs%20Nass.JPG)

*Table 81 Matt Nass vs Marc Lalague* 
After Matt Nass won a long, drawn out game one, Marc was able to come back and take the second game... Just in time for the round to end, leaving the players with an unintentional draw that knocked them both out of day two.




---
